style=\"font-size: 14px\">\n\t\tCallerCenter.com is a free consumer complaints board for reporting telephone calls.\n\t\tReport suspicious phone numbers to the world. Use the search box to see if someone has already reported the number.\n\t\tAfter filing a complaint here, we suggest you also <a href=\"/complaint/filingacomplaint.html\">file a complaint with the authorities</a> and learn how to <a href=\"/articles/getnameandaddress.html\">get the caller's name and address</a>.\n\t\tMake your voice be heard.\n\t</p>\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"panel name=\"us\"></a>\n<div class=\"panel panel-default\">\n\t<div class=\"panel-body\">\n\t\t<h2>United States: National Do Not Call Registry</h2>\n\t\t\n\t\t\t\t<p>\n\t\t\tWhile the DNC list is not growing at the same rate as when it first launched in 2003, more and more people are signing up every day.\n\t\t\tAt the end of 2010, the FCC report estimates approximately 672 million phone numbers are assigned to a person or company.\n\t\t\tThe FTC also estimates that over 183 million numbers were on the National Do Not Call list by 2010.\n\t\t\tFrom these numbers, it is estimated that over 25% of the assigned phone numbers in the US are signed up for the National Registry.\n\t\t\tA report by the Bush Administration in 2007 estimates that up to 72% of Americans had registered on the list.\n\t\t\tDuring the same period, the CTIA estimates approximately 303 million of those phone numbers were wireless meaning that approximately 45% of issued numbers are wireless.\n\t\t\tWhile wireless numbers do not need to be included on the registry to avoid unsolicited calls, consumers may still add their wireless number to the list.\n\t\t\tFCC regulations prohibit the use of automatic dialers from calling cellular numbes under any circumstance.\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/complaint/donotcallhow.html\">Learn more about the Do Not Call list including how to sign up</a>.\n\t\t\tSince 2005, any number added to the Natiional Registry will remain unless the number becomes invalid, disconnected, reassigned, or the owner of the number requests removal.\n\t\t</p>\n\t\t<div 255);\"></path></svg></div></div></div>\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\n\n\t\t\t\t<h3>Recorded Messages: The Rise of the Robocall</h3>\n\t\t<p>\n\t\t\tWhile the growth of new registrations has slowed, the number of complaints filed is growing every year.\n\t\t\tOver 5 million complaints were filed with the FTC in 2016 - more than ever before.\n\t\t</p>\n\t\t<p>\n\t\t\tOn September 1, 2009, the National Registry began accepting all complaints regarding calls using a recorded message, regardless of the registration status of the called number.\n\t\t\tAs you can see from the graphs below, a great deal of those complaints were filed against auto-dialed calls that play a recorded message (aka. robocalls).\n\t\t\tWhile around 43% of complaints reported in 2010 were due to robocalls, that percentage skyrocketed over the next few years to 64% in 2016.\n\t\t</p>\n\t\t<div class=\"row\">\n\t\t\t<div class=\"col-md-6\">\n\t\t\t\t<h3>Total Complaints by Year</h3>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"hidden-xs\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"D3ChartOuterContainer\"><div class=\"D3ChartContainer\"><div class=\"D3SizingContainer\"><svg id=\"BarChart4\" class=\"BarChart\"></svg></div></div></div>\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"visible-xs\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"D3ChartOuterContainer\"><div class=\"D3ChartContainer\"><div class=\"D3SizingContainer\"><svg id=\"BarChart5\" class=\"BarChart\"></svg></div></div></div>\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t<div class=\"col-md-6\">\n\t\t\t\t<h3>Complaints for Recorded Messages</h3>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"hidden-xs\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"D3ChartOuterContainer\"><div class=\"D3ChartContainer\"><div class=\"D3SizingContainer\"><svg id=\"BarChart6\" class=\"BarChart\"></svg></div></div></div>\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"visible-xs\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<div class=\"D3ChartOuterContainer\"><div class=\"D3ChartContainer\"><div class=\"D3SizingContainer\"><svg id=\"BarChart7\" class=\"BarChart\"></svg></div></div></div>\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t<p><small>* Stats are only available prior to Oct 2016. The remainder of the year is estimated.</small></p>\n\t\t<h3>Exceptions</h3>\n\t\t<p>The DNC list will not stop all unsolicited calls. The following types of calls are still legal.</p>\n\t\t<ul>\n\t\t\t<li>The registry applies to residential lines only (no business lines can be registered)</li>\n\t\t\t<li>Calls from political organizations</li>\n\t\t\t<li>Calls from non-profits</li>\n\t\t\t<li>Calls for surveys</li>\n\t\t\t<li>Calls from companies which the consumer contacted in the past 31 days unless the company is asked not to call</li>\n\t\t\t<li>Calls from debt collectors</li>\n\t\t</ul>\n\t\t\t</div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"panel panel-default\" id=\"ca\">\n\t<div class=\"panel-body\">\n\t\t<h2>Canada: National Do Not Call List</h2>\n\t\t<p>\n\t\t\tThe Canadian Do Not Call list has been administered by the Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission (CRTC) since 2006.\n\t\t\tLike the DNC list in the US, phone numbers do not need to be resubmitted, but there are exemptions for some unsolicited calls like charities, political organizations, pollsters, and businesses with a prior relationship just like in the US.\n\t\t\tIn addition to registering with the national list, Canadians are encouraged to request to be added to each internal company's list of numbers not to call each time they receive an unwanted call.\n\t\t\t<a href=\"https://www.lnnte-dncl.gc.ca/insnum-regnum-eng\">Click here</a> to add your number to DNC CA\n\t\t</p>\n\t</div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"panel panel-default\" id=\"uk\">\n\t<div class=\"panel-body\">\n\t\t<h2>United Kingdom: Telephone Preference Service (TPS)</h2>\n\t\t<p>\n\t\t\tThe TPS was introduced in 2009 and revised in 2003.\n\t\t\tIt is regulated by the Office of Communications (Ofcomm), enforced by the Information Commissioner's Office (ICO), and run by the Direct Marketing Association (DMA).\n\t\t\tLike the Do Not Call lists of the US and Canada, resubmitting or renewing a number already on the list is not necessary.\n\t\t\tUnlike other countries, the TPS prohibits charities, voluntary organizations, and political parties from making calls to numbers on the TPS with prior consent to do so.\n\t\t\tHowever, exceptions do exist for debt collectors. They are not required to screen the numbers that they call through the TPS.\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/complaint/tpshowto.html\">Learn more about the Telephone Preference Service including how to sign up</a>.\n\t\t</p>\n\t</div>\n</div>\n\n<h2>Recent Complaints</h2>\n<div class=\"panel panel-default complaint-display\"><div class=\"panel-body\"><h3><a href=\"/904-497-1143.html\">904-497-1143</a></h3><p><span class=\"complaint-comment\">a few seconds ago<br>\nThis is some boiler room call center for various scams.
